        Mariana Islands
       </a>
       .

          </b>

           Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands
          </a>
         </div>

      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Northern Mariana Islands
       </b>
       , officially the
       <b>
        Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        CNMI
       </b>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">
        Chamorro
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="ch">
         Sankattan Siha Na Islas Mariånas
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Carolinian_language" title="Carolinian language">
        Refaluwasch or Carolinian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        Commonwealth Téél Falúw kka Efáng llól Marianas
       </i>
       ), is an insular area and
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. insular area)">
        commonwealth
       </a>
       of the United States consisting of 15 islands in the northwestern
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       . The CNMI includes all islands in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">
        Mariana Archipelago
       </a>
       except
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       which is the southernmost island of the chain and a separate U.S. territory.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">
        United States Department of the Interior
       </a>
       cites a landmass of 183.5 square miles (475.26 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
        2010 United States Census
       </a>
       , 53,883 people were living in the CNMI at that time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The vast majority of the population resides on
       <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">
        Saipan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">
        Tinian
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Rota_(island)" title="Rota (island)">
        Rota
       </a>
       . The other islands of the Northern Marianas are sparsely inhabited; the most notable among these is
       <a href="/wiki/Pagan_(island)" title="Pagan (island)">
        Pagan
       </a>
       , which for various reasons over the centuries has experienced major population flux, but formerly had residents numbering in the thousands.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PaganMil_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PaganMil-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pagan8_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pagan8-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The administrative center is
       <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Hill,_Saipan" title="Capitol Hill, Saipan">
        Capitol Hill
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_populated_places_in_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="List of populated places in the Northern Mariana Islands">
        village
       </a>
       in northwestern
       <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">
        Saipan
       </a>
       . However, most publications consider Saipan to be the capital because the island is governed as a single municipality.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_of_humans">
        Arrival of humans
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Arrival of humans">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The first people of the Mariana Islands immigrated at some point between 4000 BC and 2000 BC from
       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </a>
       . After first contact with Spaniards, they eventually became known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">
        Chamorros
       </a>
       , a Spanish word similar to Chamori, the name of the indigenous caste system's higher division.
      </p>
      <p>
       The ancient people of the Marianas raised colonnades of megalithic capped pillars called
       <a href="/wiki/Latte_stone" title="Latte stone">
        latte stones
       </a>
       upon which they built their homes. The Spanish reported that by the time of their arrival, the largest of these were already in ruins, and that the Chamorros believed the ancestors who had erected the pillars lived in an era when people possessed supernatural abilities.
      </p>
      <p>
       Archeologists in 2013 posited that the first people to settle in the Marianas may have made what was at that point the longest uninterrupted ocean-crossing voyage in human history, and that archeological evidence indicates
       <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">
        Tinian
       </a>
       may have been the first Pacific island outside of Asia to have been settled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voyage_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-voyage-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_possession">
        Spanish possession
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Spanish possession">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG/160px-Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG/240px-Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG/320px-Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Spanish_Church_Tower.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Colonial tower, a vestige of the former Spanish colony
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first European explorer of the area, the Portuguese navigator
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
        Ferdinand Magellan
       </a>
       , arrived in 1521. He landed on Guam, the southernmost island of the Marianas, and claimed the archipelago for
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       . The Spanish ships were met offshore by the native Chamorros, who delivered refreshments and then helped themselves to a small boat belonging to Magellan's fleet. This led to a cultural clash: in Chamorro tradition, little property was private and taking something one needed, such as a boat for fishing, did not count as stealing. The Spanish did not understand this custom, and fought the Chamorros until the boat was recovered. Three days after he had been welcomed on his arrival, Magellan fled the archipelago. Spain regarded the islands as annexed and later made them part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">
        Spanish East Indies
       </a>
       (1565). In 1734, the Spanish built a royal palace in Guam for the governor of the islands. Its remains are visible even in the 21st century; see the
       <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Hag%C3%A5t%C3%B1a)" title="Plaza de España (Hagåtña)">
        Plaza de España (Hagåtña)
       </a>
       article.
      </p>
      <p>
       Guam operated as an important stopover between Manila and Mexico for galleons carrying gold between the Philippines and Spain. Some galleons sunk in Guam remain.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1668, Father
       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Luis_de_San_Vitores" title="Diego Luis de San Vitores">
        Diego Luis de San Vitores
       </a>
       renamed the islands
       <i>
        Las Marianas
       </i>
       in honor of his patroness the Spanish regent
       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_of_Austria" title="Mariana of Austria">
        Mariana of Austria
       </a>
       (1634–1696), widow of
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">
        Felipe IV
       </a>
       (reigned 1621–1655).
      </p>
      <p>
       Most of the islands' native population (90–95%)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       died from Spanish diseases or married non-Chamorro settlers under Spanish rule. New settlers, primarily from the Philippines and the Caroline Islands, were brought
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (August 2016)">
           by whom?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       to repopulate the islands. The Chamorro population gradually recovered, and Chamorro,
       <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">
        Filipino
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Carolinian_language" title="Carolinian language">
        Refaluwasch
       </a>
       languages and other ethnic differences remain in the Marianas.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 17th century, Spanish colonists forcibly moved the Chamorros to Guam, to encourage assimilation and conversion to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       . By the time they were allowed to return to the Northern Marianas, many Carolinians from present-day eastern
       <a href="/wiki/Yap_State" title="Yap State">
        Yap State
       </a>
       and western
       <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">
        Chuuk State
       </a>
       had settled in the Marianas.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Both languages, as well as English, are now official in the Commonwealth.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Carolinian_immigration">
        Carolinian immigration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Carolinian immigration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The Northern Marianas experienced an influx of immigration from the
       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">
        Carolines
       </a>
       during the 19th century. Both this Carolinian subethnicity and Carolinians in the Carolines archipelago
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">
        refer to themselves
       </a>
       as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refaluwasch" title="Refaluwasch">
        Refaluwasch
       </a>
       . The indigenous Chamoru word for the same group of people is
       <i>
        gu'palao
       </i>
       . They are usually referred to simply as "Carolinians", though unlike the other two monikers, this can also mean those who actually live in the Carolines and who may have no affiliation with the Marianas.
      </p>
      <p>
       The conquering Spanish did not focus attempts at cultural suppression against Carolinian immigrants, whose immigration they allowed during a period when the indigenous Chamoru majority was being subjugated with land alienation, forced relocations and internment. Carolinians in the Marianas continue to be fluent in the language
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words">
          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (August 2016)">
           which?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       , and have maintained many of the cultural distinctions and traditions of their ethnicity's land of ancestral origin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cunningham1_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cunningham1-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
          <span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (August 2016)">
           need quotation to verify
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="German_and_Japanese_possession">
        German and Japanese possession
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: German and Japanese possession">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="525" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG/220px-Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG/330px-Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG/440px-Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Korean_Cafe_in_Saipan.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Saipan under the administration of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Empire" title="Japanese Empire">
          Japan
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following its loss during the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       of 1898,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spain
       </a>
       ceded Guam to the United States and sold the remainder of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">
        Marianas
       </a>
       (i.e., the Northern Marianas), along with the Caroline Islands, to
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        Germany
       </a>
       under the
       <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Spanish_Treaty_(1899)" title="German–Spanish Treaty (1899)">
        German–Spanish Treaty of 1899
       </a>
       . Germany administered the islands as part of its colony of
       <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">
        German New Guinea
       </a>
       and did little in terms of development.
      </p>
      <p>
       Early in
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       declared war on Germany and invaded the Northern Marianas. In 1919, the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       awarded all of Germany's islands in the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       located north of the
       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">
        Equator
       </a>
       , including the Northern Marianas, under
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">
        mandate
       </a>
       to Japan. Under this arrangement, the Japanese thus administered the Northern Marianas as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Mandate" title="South Pacific Mandate">
        South Pacific Mandate
       </a>
       . During the Japanese period,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">
        sugar cane
       </a>
       became the main industry of the islands.
       <a href="/wiki/Garapan" title="Garapan">
        Garapan
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">
        Saipan
       </a>
       was developed as a regional capital, and numerous Japanese (including ethnic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_people" title="Korean people">
        Koreans
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">
        Okinawan
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_people" title="Taiwanese people">
        Taiwanese
       </a>
       ) migrated to the islands. In the December 1939 census, the total population of the South Pacific Mandate was 129,104, of whom 77,257 were Japanese (including ethnic Taiwanese and Koreans). On Saipan the pre-war population comprised 29,348 Japanese settlers and 3,926 Chamorro and Caroline Islanders;
       <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">
        Tinian
       </a>
       had 15,700 Japanese settlers (including 2,700 ethnic Koreans and 22 ethnic Chamorro).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">
        World War II
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: World War II">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On December 8, 1941, hours after the
       <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">
        attack on Pearl Harbor
       </a>
       , Japanese forces from the Marianas launched an
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guam_(1941)" title="Battle of Guam (1941)">
        invasion of Guam
       </a>
       . Chamorros from the Northern Marianas, which had been under Japanese rule for more than 20 years, were brought to Guam to assist the Japanese administration. This, combined with the harsh treatment of Guamanian Chamorros during the 31-month occupation, created a rift that would become the main reason Guamanians rejected the reunification referendum approved by the Northern Marianas in the 1960s.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg/220px-Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg/330px-Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg/440px-Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marine_infantrymen_on_Saipan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Marine infantrymen in
         <a href="/wiki/Garapan" title="Garapan">
          Garapan
         </a>
         , Saipan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On June 15, 1944, near the end of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , the United States military invaded the Mariana Islands, starting the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saipan" title="Battle of Saipan">
        Battle of Saipan
       </a>
       , which ended on July 9. Of the 30,000 Japanese troops defending Saipan, fewer than 1,000 remained alive at the battle's end.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Over 20,000 Japanese civilians were also killed, or committed suicide rather than be captured.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       U.S. forces then recaptured Guam on July 21, and
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tinian" title="Battle of Tinian">
        invaded Tinian
       </a>
       on July 24; a year later
       <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">
        Tinian
       </a>
       was the takeoff point for the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Enola_Gay" title="Enola Gay">
         Enola Gay
        </a>
       </i>
       , the plane that dropped the atomic bomb on
       <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">
        Hiroshima
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Rota_(island)" title="Rota (island)">
        Rota
       </a>
       was left untouched (and isolated) until the Japanese surrender in August 1945, owing to its military insignificance.
      </p>
      <p>
       The war did not end for everyone with the signing of the armistice. The last group of
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_holdout" title="Japanese holdout">
        Japanese holdouts
       </a>
       surrendered on Saipan on December 1, 1945. On Guam, Japanese soldier
       <a href="/wiki/Shoichi_Yokoi" title="Shoichi Yokoi">
        Shoichi Yokoi
       </a>
       , unaware that the war had ended, hid in a jungle cave in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talofofo" title="Talofofo">
        Talofofo
       </a>
       area until 1972.
      </p>
      <p>
       Japanese nationals were eventually repatriated to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_home_islands" title="Japanese home islands">
        Japanese home islands
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="United_States_Territory_.28Commonwealth.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Territory_(Commonwealth)">
        United States Territory (Commonwealth)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United States Territory (Commonwealth)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">
        Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saipan.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Saipan.jpg/220px-Saipan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Saipan.jpg/330px-Saipan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Saipan.jpg/440px-Saipan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saipan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The island of
         <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">
          Saipan
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After Japan's defeat in World War II, the Northern Marianas were administered by the United States pursuant to
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_21" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 21">
        Security Council Resolution 21
       </a>
       as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">
        Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands
       </a>
       , which gave responsibility for defense and foreign affairs to the United States. Four referenda offering integration with Guam or changes to the islands' status were held in
       <a href="/wiki/Saipan_integration_referendum,_1958" title="Saipan integration referendum, 1958">
        1958
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands_status_referendum,_1961" title="Northern Mariana Islands status referendum, 1961">
        1961
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saipan_integration_referendum,_1963" title="Saipan integration referendum, 1963">
        1963
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands_status_referendum,_1969" title="Northern Mariana Islands status referendum, 1969">
        1969
       </a>
       . On each occasion, a majority voted in favor of integration with Guam, but this did not happen: Guam rejected integration in a
       <a href="/wiki/Guamanian_Northern_Mariana_Islands_union_referendum,_1969" title="Guamanian Northern Mariana Islands union referendum, 1969">
        1969 referendum
       </a>
       . The people of the Northern Mariana Islands decided in the 1970s not to seek independence, but instead to forge closer links with the United States. Negotiations for
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. insular area)">
        commonwealth status
       </a>
       began in 1972 and a covenant to establish a commonwealth in political union with the United States
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was approved in a
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands_status_referendum,_1975" title="Northern Mariana Islands status referendum, 1975">
        1975 referendum
       </a>
       . A new government and constitution came into effect in 1978 after being approved in a
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands_constitutional_referendum,_1977" title="Northern Mariana Islands constitutional referendum, 1977">
        1977 referendum
       </a>
       . The United Nations approved this arrangement pursuant to
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_683" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 683">
        Security Council Resolution 683
       </a>
       . The Commonwealth does not have voting representation in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
        United States Congress
       </a>
       , but, since 2009, has been represented in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">
        U.S. House of Representatives
       </a>
       by a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delegate_(United_States_Congress)" title="Delegate (United States Congress)">
        delegate
       </a>
       who may participate in debate but may not vote on the floor. The Commonwealth has no representation in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
        U.S. Senate
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anatahan_aerial.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="640" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Anatahan_aerial.jpg/220px-Anatahan_aerial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Anatahan_aerial.jpg/330px-Anatahan_aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Anatahan_aerial.jpg/440px-Anatahan_aerial.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anatahan_aerial.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Anatahan" title="Anatahan">
          Anatahan
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northern_Mariana_Islands_map.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="371" data-file-width="345" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Northern_Mariana_Islands_map.gif/220px-Northern_Mariana_Islands_map.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Northern_Mariana_Islands_map.gif/330px-Northern_Mariana_Islands_map.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/26/Northern_Mariana_Islands_map.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Northern_Mariana_Islands_map.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the Northern Mariana Islands.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Extreme_points_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Extreme points of the Northern Mariana Islands">
        Extreme points of the Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Northern Mariana Islands, together with
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       to the south, compose the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">
        Mariana Islands
       </a>
       archipelago. The southern islands are
       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">
        limestone
       </a>
       , with level terraces and fringing
       <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">
        coral
       </a>
       reefs. The northern islands are volcanic, with active
       <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">
        volcanoes
       </a>
       on several islands, including
       <a href="/wiki/Anatahan" title="Anatahan">
        Anatahan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pagan_Island" title="Pagan Island">
        Pagan
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Agrihan" title="Agrihan">
        Agrihan
       </a>
       . The volcano on Agrihan has the highest elevation at 3,166 feet (965 m).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Anatahan Volcano is a small volcanic island 80 miles (130 km) north of Saipan. It is about 6 miles (10 km) long and 2 miles (3 km) wide. Anatahan began erupting from its east crater on May 10, 2003. It has since alternated between eruptive and calm periods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On April 6, 2005, an estimated 50,000,000 cubic feet (1,416,000 m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       ) of ash and rock were ejected, causing a large, black cloud to drift south over Saipan and Tinian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Northern Mariana Islands have a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">
        tropical rainforest climate
       </a>
       moderated by seasonal northeast
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">
        trade winds
       </a>
       , with little seasonal temperature variation. The dry season runs from December to June; the rainy season runs from July to November and can include
       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">
        typhoons
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" title="Guinness Book of World Records">
         Guinness Book of World Records
        </a>
       </i>
       has said Saipan has the most
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/equable" title="wikt:equable">
        equable
       </a>
       climate in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">
        Politics and government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics and government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Politics of the Northern Mariana Islands">
        Politics of the Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benigno_Fitial.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="305" data-file-width="247" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Benigno_Fitial.jpg/220px-Benigno_Fitial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d4/Benigno_Fitial.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benigno_Fitial.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Fitial" title="Benigno Fitial">
          Benigno Fitial
         </a>
         , the former
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Governor of the Northern Mariana Islands">
          Governor of the Northern Mariana Islands
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Northern Mariana Islands have a
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">
        multiparty
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">
        presidential
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       system. They are a commonwealth of the United States. Federal funds to the commonwealth are administered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Insular_Affairs" title="Office of Insular Affairs">
        Office of Insular Affairs
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_the_Interior" title="U.S. Department of the Interior">
        U.S. Department of the Interior
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Replicating the separation of powers elsewhere in the United States, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">
        executive branch
       </a>
       is headed by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Northern_Mariana_Islands_Governors" title="List of Northern Mariana Islands Governors">
        Governor of the Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">
        legislative power
       </a>
       is vested in the bicameral
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands_Commonwealth_Legislature" title="Northern Mariana Islands Commonwealth Legislature">
        Northern Mariana Islands Commonwealth Legislature
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
        judicial power
       </a>
       is vested in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Commonwealth_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Supreme Court of the Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands">
        CNMI Supreme Court
       </a>
       and the trial courts inferior to it.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some critics, including the author of the political website
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Saipan_Sucks" title="Saipan Sucks">
         Saipan Sucks
        </a>
       </i>
       , say that politics in the Northern Mariana Islands is often "more a function of family relationships and personal loyalties" where the size of one's extended family is more important than a candidate's personal qualifications. They charge that this is
       <a href="/wiki/Nepotism" title="Nepotism">
        nepotism
       </a>
       carried out within the trappings of democracy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reyes_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Reyes-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In April 2012, anticipating a loss of funding by 2014, the Commonwealth's
       <a href="/wiki/Pension_fund#Public_vs._private_pension_funds" title="Pension fund">
        public pension fund
       </a>
       declared
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chapter_11_bankruptcy" title="Chapter 11 bankruptcy">
        Chapter 11 bankruptcy
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The retirement fund is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defined_benefit" title="Defined benefit">
        defined benefit
       </a>
       -type pension plan and was only partially funded by the government, with only $268.4 million in
       <a href="/wiki/Asset" title="Asset">
        assets
       </a>
       and $911 million in
       <a href="/wiki/Liability_(financial_accounting)" title="Liability (financial accounting)">
        liabilities
       </a>
       . The plan experienced low investment returns and a benefit structure that had been increased without raises in funding.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p&amp;i20120419_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-p&amp;i20120419-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In August 2012, cries for impeachment
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       arose, as the sitting governor
       <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Fitial" title="Benigno Fitial">
        Benigno Fitial
       </a>
       was being held responsible for withholding payments from the pension fund,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       not paying the local utility (Commonwealth Utilities or "CUC") for government offices,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       cutting off funding to the only hospital in the Northern Marianas,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       interfering with the delivery of a
       <a href="/wiki/Subpoena" title="Subpoena">
        subpoena
       </a>
       to his attorney general,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       withholding required funds from the public schools,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and for signing a sole source $190 million contract for power generation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Political party strength in the Northern Mariana Islands">
        Political party strength in the Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>

        <tr>
         <td colspan="9" style="text-align:left; background:#fff;">
          <dl>
           <dt>
            Notes
           </dt>
          </dl>
          <div class="refbegin" style="">
           <div class="mw-references-wrap">
            <ol class="references">
             <li id="cite_note-31">
              <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         </td>

       </table>
      </center>
      <p>
       Administratively, the CNMI is divided into four
       <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">
        municipalities
       </a>
       :
      </p>
      <p>
       The Northern Islands (north of Saipan) form the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Islands_Municipality" title="Northern Islands Municipality">
        Northern Islands Municipality
       </a>
       . The three main islands of the Southern Islands form the municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">
        Saipan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">
        Tinian
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Rota_(island)" title="Rota (island)">
        Rota
       </a>
       , with uninhabited Aguijan forming part of Tinian municipality.
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of volcanic threat, the northern islands have been evacuated. Human habitation was limited to Agrihan, Pagan, and Alamagan, but population varied due to various economic factors, including children's education. The 2010 census showed no residents in Northern Islands municipality and the Northern Islands' mayor office is located in "exile" on Saipan.
      </p>
      <p>
       Saipan, Tinian, and Rota have the only ports and harbors, and are the only permanently populated islands.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_status">
        Political status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1947, the Northern Mariana Islands became part of the post–World War II United Nations
       <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">
        Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands
       </a>
       (TTPI). The United States became the TTPI's administering authority under the terms of a trusteeship agreement. In 1976, Congress approved the mutually negotiated
       <a class="external text" href="http://cnmilaw.org/cnmicovenant.html" rel="nofollow">
        Covenant to establish a Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands in Political Union with the United States of America
       </a>
       . The Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands (CNMI) government adopted its own constitution in 1977, and the constitutional government took office in January 1978. The Covenant was fully implemented on November 3, 1986, pursuant to Presidential Proclamation no. 5564, which conferred United States citizenship on legally qualified CNMI residents. This led to CNMI being represented in the United States (and especially Washington, D.C.) by a
       <i>
        Resident Representative
       </i>
       who was elected at-large by CNMI voters and whose office was paid for by the CNMI government. The
       <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_Natural_Resources_Act_of_2008" title="Consolidated Natural Resources Act of 2008">
        Consolidated Natural Resources Act of 2008
       </a>
       ("CNRA"), approved by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">
        U.S. Congress
       </a>
       on May 8, 2008, established a CNMI delegate's seat; Democrat
       <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Sablan" title="Gregorio Sablan">
        Gregorio Sablan
       </a>
       was elected in
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_2008" title="United States House of Representatives elections, 2008">
        November 2008
       </a>
       as the first CNMI delegate and took office in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/111th_Congress" title="111th Congress">
        111th Congress
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On December 22, 1990, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">
        United Nations Trusteeship Council
       </a>
       terminated the TTPI as it applied to the CNMI and five other of the TTPI's original seven districts (the
       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">
        Marshall Islands
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">
        Federated States of Micronesia
       </a>
       (Chuuk, Kosrae, Pohnpei and Yap)), this was acknowledged in
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_683" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 683">
        United Nations Security Council Resolution 683
       </a>
       passed on the same day.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="626" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg/220px-TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg/330px-TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg/440px-TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TTPI_High_Court_judges.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         TTPI High Court judges
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Under the Covenant, in general, United States federal law applies to CNMI. However, the CNMI is outside the customs territory of the United States and, although the internal revenue code does apply in the form of a local income tax, the income tax system is largely locally determined. According to the Covenant, the federal minimum wage and federal immigration laws "will not apply to the Northern Mariana Islands except in the manner and to the extent made applicable to them by the Congress by law after termination of the Trusteeship Agreement."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The local control of minimum wage was superseded by the United States Congress in 2007.
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to November 28, 2009, U.S. immigration laws did not apply in the CNMI. Rather, a separate immigration system existed in the CNMI. This system was established under the Covenant to Establish a Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands in Political Union with the United States of America ("Covenant"), which was signed in 1975 and codified as 48 U.S.C. § 1801. The Covenant was unilaterally amended by the CNRA, thus altering the CNMI's immigration system. Specifically, CNRA § 702(a) amended the Covenant to state that "the provisions of the 'immigration laws' (as defined in section 101(a)(17) of the Immigration and Nationality Act (8 U.S.C. 1101(a)(17))) shall apply to the Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands." Further, under CNRA § 702(a), the "immigration laws," as well as the amendments to the Covenant, "shall...supersede and replace all laws, provisions, or programs of the Commonwealth relating to the admission of aliens and the removal of aliens from the Commonwealth."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Transition to U.S. immigration laws began November 28, 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ST_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ST-39">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The CNMI has a
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_territorial_court" title="United States territorial court">
        United States territorial court
       </a>
       which exercises jurisdiction over the District of the Northern Mariana Islands (DNMI), which is coterminous with the CNMI. The
       <a href="/wiki/District_Court_for_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="District Court for the Northern Mariana Islands">
        District Court for the Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
       was established by
       <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Congress" title="Act of Congress">
        act of Congress
       </a>
       in 1977, and began operations in January 1978. The court sits on the island of
       <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">
        Saipan
       </a>
       , but may sit other places within the Commonwealth. The district court has the same jurisdiction as all other United States district courts, including diversity jurisdiction and
       <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">
        bankruptcy
       </a>
       jurisdiction. Appeals are taken to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">
        Ninth Circuit
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Economy of the Northern Mariana Islands">
        Economy of the Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pagan_Island,_Northern_Marianas.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1440" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pagan_Island%2C_Northern_Marianas.jpg/220px-Pagan_Island%2C_Northern_Marianas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pagan_Island%2C_Northern_Marianas.jpg/330px-Pagan_Island%2C_Northern_Marianas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pagan_Island%2C_Northern_Marianas.jpg/440px-Pagan_Island%2C_Northern_Marianas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pagan_Island,_Northern_Marianas.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pagan_Island" title="Pagan Island">
          Pagan Island
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands benefits from its trading relationship with the federal government of the United States and cheap trained labor from Asia. Historically, the CNMI's economy has relied on tourism, mostly from Japan, and on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garment" title="Garment">
        garment
       </a>
       manufacturing sector. The economy has declined since quotas were lifted in 2005, eventually leading all the garment factories on Saipan to close by February 2009. Tourism also declined after 2005 when
       <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">
        Japan Airlines
       </a>
       stopped serving the Marianas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Business_Law_Handbook_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Business_Law_Handbook-40">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Northern Mariana Islands had successfully used its position as a free trade area with the U.S., while at the same time not being subject to the same
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_laws" title="Labor laws">
        labor laws
       </a>
       . For example, the $3.05 per hour minimum wage in the Commonwealth, which lasted from 1997 to 2007, was lower than in the U.S. and some other worker protections are weaker, leading to lower production costs. That allowed garments to be labeled "Made in USA" without having to comply with all U.S. labor laws. However, the U.S. minimum wage law signed by President Bush on May 25, 2007, resulted in stepped increases in the Northern Marianas' minimum wage, which will allow it to reach the U.S. level by 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vallejera_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Vallejera-41">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first step (to $3.55) became effective July 25, 2007, and a yearly increase of $0.50 will take effect every May thereafter until the CNMI minimum wage equals the nationwide minimum wage. However, a law signed by President Obama in December 2009 delayed the yearly increase from May to September. As of September 30, 2014, the minimum wage is $6.05 per hour.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The island's exemption from U.S. labor laws had led to many alleged exploitations including recent claims of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweatshops" title="Sweatshops">
        sweatshops
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_labor" title="Child labor">
        child labor
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Child_prostitution" title="Child prostitution">
        child prostitution
       </a>
       , and even forced abortions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TomPaine_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TomPaine-43">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarren_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Clarren-44">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An immigration system mostly outside of federal U.S. control (which ended on November 28, 2009) resulted in a large number of Chinese migrant workers (about 15,000 during the peak years) employed in the islands' garment trade. However, the lifting of
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        World Trade Organization
       </a>
       restrictions on Chinese imports to the U.S. in 2005 had put the Commonwealth-based trade under severe pressure, leading to a number of recent factory closures. Adding to the U.S.-imposed scheduled wage increases, the garment industry became extinct by 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Agricultural production, primarily of
       <a href="/wiki/Tapioca" title="Tapioca">
        tapioca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">
        cattle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">
        coconuts
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">
        breadfruit
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">
        tomatoes
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Melon" title="Melon">
        melons
       </a>
       exists but is relatively unimportant in the economy.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Non-native islanders are not allowed to own land, but can lease it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The islands have over 220 miles (350 km) of highways, three airports with paved runways (one about 9,800 feet [3,000 m] long; two around 6,600 feet [2,000 m]), three airports with unpaved runways, and one heliport. The main commercial airport is
       <a href="/wiki/Saipan_International_Airport" title="Saipan International Airport">
        Saipan International Airport
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Mail service for the islands is provided by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">
        U.S. Postal Service
       </a>
       (USPS). Each major island has its own zip code in the 96950–96952 range, and the USPS two-letter abbreviation for the CNMI is "MP".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNMI-LRC_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNMI-LRC-47">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USPS-abbrs_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-USPS-abbrs-48">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For phone service, the islands are included in the
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">
        North American Numbering Plan
       </a>
       , using
       <a href="/wiki/Area_code_670" title="Area code 670">
        area code 670
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNMI-LRC_47-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNMI-LRC-47">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Television service is provided by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KPPI-LP" title="KPPI-LP">
        KPPI-LP
       </a>
       , Channel 7, which simulcasts Guam's
       <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
        ABC
       </a>
       affiliate
       <a href="/wiki/KTGM" title="KTGM">
        KTGM
       </a>
       , as well as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WSZE" title="WSZE">
        WSZE
       </a>
       , Channel 10, which simulcasts Guam's
       <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">
        NBC
       </a>
       affiliate
       <a href="/wiki/KUAM-TV" title="KUAM-TV">
        KUAM-TV
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="List of radio stations in the Northern Mariana Islands">
        About 10 radio stations
       </a>
       broadcast within the CNMI.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Demographics of the Northern Mariana Islands">
        Demographics of the Northern Mariana Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">
        List of U.S. states and territories by population
       </a>
      </div>
