      <p>
       According to the 2010 census, the population of the CNMI as of April 1, 2010, was 53,883, down from 69,221 in 2000, a decrease of 22.2%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The decrease was reportedly due to a combination of factors including the demise of the garment industry (the vast majority of whose employees were females from China), economic crises, and a decline in tourism, one of the CNMI's primary sources of revenue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ST_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ST-39">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Except for the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands" title="United States Minor Outlying Islands">
        U.S. Minor Outlying Islands
       </a>
       , the Northern Mariana Islands are the least populous sub-federal jurisdiction in the United States, with fewer people than any of the 50 states, the other commonwealth and three self-governing territories, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia">
        District of Columbia
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Asian (including Filipino, Chinese, Korean, Japanese, Bangladeshi and other Asian) 49.9%
       </li>
       <li>
        Chamorro, Carolinian, Palauan and Other Pacific Islander 34.9%
       </li>
       <li>
        Multiracial 12.7%
       </li>
       <li>
        Others 2.5%
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">
        Pew Research Center
       </a>
       , 2010:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
         Roman Catholic
        </a>
        64.1%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
         Protestants
        </a>
        16%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">
         Buddhists
        </a>
        10.6%
       </li>
       <li>
        Folk religions 5.3%
       </li>
       <li>
        Other Christians 1.2%
       </li>
       <li>
        Other religions 1.1%
       </li>
       <li>
        Unaffiliated 1.0%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox">
         Eastern Orthodox
        </a>
        &lt;1%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
         Hindu
        </a>
        &lt;1%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
         Muslim
        </a>
        &lt;1%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
         Jews
        </a>
        &lt;1%
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands_Public_School_System" title="Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands Public School System">
        Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands Public School System
       </a>
       operates public schools in the commonwealth and there are numerous private schools.
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Marianas_College" title="Northern Marianas College">
        Northern Marianas College
       </a>
       is accredited by the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="Western Association of Schools and Colleges">
        Western Association of Schools and Colleges
       </a>
       and offers a range of programs similar to other small U.S.
       <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">
        community colleges
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chamorro_performers.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Chamorro_performers.jpg/190px-Chamorro_performers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Chamorro_performers.jpg/285px-Chamorro_performers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Chamorro_performers.jpg/380px-Chamorro_performers.jpg 2x" width="190"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chamorro_performers.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Chamorro people
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Much of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">
        Chamorro
       </a>
       culture in the Mariana Islands was heavily influenced by the Spanish during the Spanish era, as well as by the Germans and Japanese. In Chamorro culture, respect is the biggest thing taught, and one common display is the tradition of "manngingi'". This tradition has been around for centuries and involves an elder and a young Chamorro child. The child takes the hand of the elder, places it on their nose and says
       <i>
        ñot
       </i>
       to the men and
       <i>
        ñora
       </i>
       to the women with the elders responding
       <i>
        diosti ayudi
       </i>
       , meaning "God help you".
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Carolinian_people" title="Carolinian people">
        Carolinian
       </a>
       culture is very similar to the Chamorro culture with respect being very important. The Carolinian culture can be traced back to
       <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">
        Yap
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_Lagoon" title="Chuuk Lagoon">
        Chuuk
       </a>
       , where the Carolinians originated.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Much of Chamorro cuisine is influenced by various cultures. Examples of popular foods of foreign origin include various types of sweet or savory
       <a href="/wiki/Empanada" title="Empanada">
        empanada
       </a>
       , originally introduced from Spain, and
       <a href="/wiki/Pancit" title="Pancit">
        pancit
       </a>
       , a noodle dish from the Philippines.
      </p>
      <p>
       Archeological evidence reveals that rice has been cultivated in the Marianas since prehistoric times. Red rice made with achoti is a distinct staple food that strongly distinguishes Chamorro cuisine from that of other Pacific islands. It is commonly served for special events, such as parties (gupot or "fiestas"), novenas, and high school or college graduations. Fruits such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lemmai" title="Lemmai">
        lemmai
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">
        mangga
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Niyok&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Niyok (page does not exist)">
        niyok
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Averrhoa_bilimbi" title="Averrhoa bilimbi">
        bilimbines
       </a>
       are included in various local recipes. Korean, Chinese, Japanese, and American cuisine are also commonly available.
      </p>
      <p>
       Local specialities include
       <a href="/wiki/Kelaguen" title="Kelaguen">
        kelaguen
       </a>
       , a dish in which meat is cooked in whole or in part by the action of
       <a href="/wiki/Citric_acid" title="Citric acid">
        citric acid
       </a>
       rather than heat; tinaktak, a meat dish made with coconut milk; and kå'du fanihi (flying fox/fruit bat soup). Fruit bats and local birds have become scarce in modern times, primarily due to the World War II-era introduction of the brown tree snake, which decimated the populations of local birds and threatens the fanihi population as well; hunting them is now illegal.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Marianas and the Hawaiian islands are the world's foremost consumers, per capita, of
       <a href="/wiki/Spam_(food)" title="Spam (food)">
        Spam
       </a>
       , with Guam at the top of the list, and Hawaii second (details regarding the rest of the Marianas are often absent from statistics). Spam was introduced to the islands by the American military as war rations during the World War II era.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion_2">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saipan_from_ISS_2.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="2500" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Saipan_from_ISS_2.png/220px-Saipan_from_ISS_2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Saipan_from_ISS_2.png/330px-Saipan_from_ISS_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Saipan_from_ISS_2.png/440px-Saipan_from_ISS_2.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saipan_from_ISS_2.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">
          Saipan
         </a>
         seen from the
         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
          International Space Station
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Owing to the Spanish
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Missionaries" title="Missionaries">
        missionaries
       </a>
       in the Marianas, a large majority of Chamorros and Carolinians practice
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       , including the use of
       <a href="/wiki/Rosary" title="Rosary">
        rosaries
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Novena" title="Novena">
        novenas
       </a>
       . The Japanese occupation had the effect of creating a sizable
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">
        Buddhist
       </a>
       community which remained even after their departure. Due to influence of the United States, diverse denominations of
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestantism
       </a>
       also entered the islands.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Mariana_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Team
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports" title="Sports">
        sports
       </a>
       popular in the United States were introduced to the Northern Mariana Islands by American soldiers during World War II.
       <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">
        Baseball
       </a>
       is the islands' most popular sport. CNMI teams have made appearances in the
       <a href="/wiki/Little_League_World_Series" title="Little League World Series">
        Little League World Series
       </a>
       (in the Little, Junior, Senior and Big league divisions) as well as winning gold medals in the
       <a href="/wiki/Micronesian_Games" title="Micronesian Games">
        Micronesian Games
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Games" title="South Pacific Games">
        South Pacific Games
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        Basketball
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts" title="Mixed martial arts">
        mixed martial arts
       </a>
       are also popular in the islands. Trench Wars is the CNMI's Mixed Martial Arts brand.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Fighters from the CNMI have competed in the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Xtreme_Combat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pacific Xtreme Combat (page does not exist)">
        Pacific Xtreme Combat
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Other sports in the CNMI include
       <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">
        volleyball
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">
        tennis
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer">
        soccer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Outrigger" title="Outrigger">
        outrigger
       </a>
       sailing,
       <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">
        softball
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Beach_volleyball" title="Beach volleyball">
        beach volleyball
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">
        rugby
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">
        golf
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">
        boxing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">
        kickboxing
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tae_kwon_do" title="Tae kwon do">
        tae kwon do
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">
        track and field
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">
        Swimming
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">
        Triathlon
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">
        American football
       </a>
       .
      </p>
